BXCEP17_COPY	PATH CEP17 Copy	Copy number of CEP17 in the pathology report. This is the number of copies of the CEP17 gene seen in the sample, which is used to calculate the HER2/CEP17 ratio. Having multiple copies of a gene means that the tumor's DNA has many consecutive repetitions of the region that codes for a given gene. Having multiple extra copies of a gene is also described as an amplification, while losing copies of a gene is described as a deletion.	STRING	SAMPLE	1				
BXHER2_COPY	PATH HER2 Copy	Copy number of HER2 in the pathology report. This is the number of copies of the HER2 gene seen in the sample, which is used to calculate the HER2/CEP17 ratio. Having multiple copies of a gene means that the tumor's DNA has many consecutive repetitions of the region that codes for a given gene. Having multiple extra copies of a gene is also described as an amplification, while losing copies of a gene is described as a deletion.	STRING	SAMPLE	1				
BXHER2_RATIO	PATH HER2 CEP17 Ratio	Ratio of HER2/CEP17 in the pathology report. This is one component of the Flourescence In Situ Hybridization (FISH) test. This ratio is used to determine if the HER2 gene is overexpressed, relative to the CEP17 protein, which acts as a baseline measurement. HER2/CEP17 ratios >2.2 indicate a HER2 Positive tumor.	STRING	SAMPLE	1

BX_HER2FISH	PATH HER2 FISH	HER2 Flourescence In Situ Hyrbridization (FISH) results in the pathology report. This is most commonly performed on tumor samples with a HER2 Immunohistochemistry (IHC) score of 2+, or equivocal. This is an additional test that aims to measure whether or not the HER2 gene is overexpressed in a tumor sample.	STRING	SAMPLE	1				
BX_HER2IHC	PATH HER2 IHC	HER2 Immunohistochemistry (IHC) results in the pathology report. This test involves staining tissue samples and looking at them under a microscope to determine if the HER2 protein is overexpressed in the sample. Results can be reported as 0+, 1+, 2+, or 3+. 0+ and 1+ indicate a HER2 negative tumor, 2+ is considered equivocal and may require further testing, and 3+ indicates a HER2 Positive tumor.	STRING	SAMPLE	1

DX_CEP17_COPY	MedR Diagnostic CEP17 Copy	Copy number of CEP17 in diagnostic sample. This is the number of copies of the CEP17 gene seen in the sample, which is used to calculate the HER2/CEP17 ratio. Having multiple copies of a gene means that the tumor's DNA has many consecutive repetitions of the region that codes for a given gene. This is an additional test that aims to measure whether or not the HER2 gene is overexpressed in a tumor sample.	STRING	PATIENT	1				
DX_HER2IHC	MedR Diagnostic HER2 IHC	HER2 Immunohistochemistry (IHC) results of diagnostic sample. This test involves staining tissue samples and looking at them under a microscope to determine if the HER2 protein is overexpressed in the sample. Results can be reported as 0+, 1+, 2+, or 3+. 0+ and 1+ indicate a HER2 negative tumor, 2+ is considered equivocal and may require further testing, and 3+ indicates a HER2 Positive tumor. GLEASON_SCORE	Radical Prostatectomy Gleason Score for Prostate Cancer	The score derived from universally embraced prostate cancer grading system developed by Dr. Donald F. Gleason in 1977. The system provides a reproducible description of the glandular architecture of prostate tissue to which a pathologist assigns a score depending primarily on the microscopic patterns of cancerous glands and cell morphology. The system correlates well with behavior at the extremes: Gleason 1+1 tumors are the most well differentiated, slowly growing and rarely spread; Gleason 4+5 tumors are the most poorly differentiated, often widely metastatic at the time of diagnosis. In the commoner intermediate grade tumors, however, behavior is extremely variable.	STRING	SAMPLE	1
